******************************************************************************************
SWGEmu "/object createitem" Command Reference (08/18/12 Edition)
Compiled by Aviin
******************************************************************************************


******************************************************************************************

Note 1:  The format of this file sucks.  I am aware of it.  It was created using "Tre
         Explorer" (http://forum.modsource.org/index.php?topic=33.0) to extract all of the
         .iff files that were "tangibles", then the folder with the extracted files was
         cataloged with a program called "DirLister"
         (http://download.cnet.com/Dirlister/3000-2248_4-10671618.html).  A few quick find
         and replace edits and many lengthy hand edits with Windows Notepad cleaned up the
         listing into a more usable (but still poorly organized) format.

         It has occured to me that this same information could have been gotten from the
         MMOCoreORB/bin/scripts/object/tangible folder of the server software.  This would
         have perhaps yielded a list that contained less non-working items.  The upside of
         this list, though, is that it contains a full list of all the tangibles that
         Pre-CU had to offer and as the server is updated in the future, more and more of
         the items in this list will work.

Note 2:  You'll note that genuine weapons are not to be found in this list.  They are not
         a part of the tangibles list and so are created through the use of the
         /GenerateCraftedItem command.  I would refer you to the excellent pdf posted by
         SWGEmu forum user Warfeather for a listing of weapon generation commands (and a
         whole lot more!).  It can be found at
         http://www.swgemu.com/forums/showthread.php?t=19&page=2&p=275640#post275640.

Note 3:  It is useful to map the paste command in SWG for ease of input of these commands.

Note 4:  Not all items are functional.  Some items may not appear in your inventory but
         will still take space; in this case, the only solution I am aware of is to use
         the /wipeitems command to delete your entire inventory, thereby destroying the
         ghost items.

******************************************************************************************
